  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e4055782-4491-401f-b4d0-fcb00a0e5c77'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer15667503892976925093"><i>In Rachel Caine's town of Morganville, "there's always a surprise just around every dark corner" - and it usually involves the undead. Now these secrets come to light in the first two books of the Morganville Vampires series, together in one volume.</i><br/><br/><br/><b>GLASS HOUSES</b><br/>Morganville is a small college town in the heart of Texas that has its share of quirky characters - and some evil </span>
  <span id="freeText15667503892976925093" style="display:none"><i>In Rachel Caine's town of Morganville, "there's always a surprise just around every dark corner" - and it usually involves the undead. Now these secrets come to light in the first two books of the Morganville Vampires series, together in one volume.</i><br /><br /><br /><b>GLASS HOUSES</b><br />Morganville is a small college town in the heart of Texas that has its share of quirky characters - and some evil ones too. When student Claire Danvers moves off campus into one of Morganville's oldest houses, she finds that her roommates don't show many signs of life. But they'll have Claire's back when the town's deepest secrets come crawling out, hungry for fresh blood.<br /><br /><br /><b>THE DEAD GIRLS' DANCE</b><br />Claire Danvers has her share of challenges - like living among creatures of the night. On the upside, she has a great roommate (who tends to disappear at sunup) and a new boyfriend. Now a fraternity is throwing its annual Dead Girls' Dance and - surprise! - Claire and her equally outcast friend have been invited. When they find out why, all hell breaks loose, because this time both the living <i>and</i> the dead are ready to tear up the night.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6344722413461604110">Okay, okay, I realize I give a lot of the books I read five stars, but what can I say, I love every one of them. Maybe it's because I pick really great books or my friends recommend them to me. Either way, I give this one 5 stars as well. <br/>The pretense was not what I expected, in a good way. I expected the vampires to be nice....uh...NO.<br/>I expected the residents in the Glass House to be vampires....uh.....NO. <br/>I expected Claire to have special abilities.....uh.....NO.<br/>I expected Shane to have a deep</span>
  <span id="freeText6344722413461604110" style="display:none">Okay, okay, I realize I give a lot of the books I read five stars, but what can I say, I love every one of them. Maybe it's because I pick really great books or my friends recommend them to me. Either way, I give this one 5 stars as well. <br />The pretense was not what I expected, in a good way. I expected the vampires to be nice....uh...NO.<br />I expected the residents in the Glass House to be vampires....uh.....NO. <br />I expected Claire to have special abilities.....uh.....NO.<br />I expected Shane to have a deep dark secret....uh.....okay, I got that one right. <br />And don't get me started on Michael. Big fat twist!<br />The mean girls aren't just mean. They're deadly!<br />This book was a page-turning thrill ride and after I finished it, I went to the store and bought volumes 2 and 3.<br />I would highly recommend this book. Anyone who enjoyed Twilight will eat this one up.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7535129899445735260">So, I was totally srprised by how much I LOVED these books! I checked them out of my library warily because I've been so burned out on vampires after the recent craze in YA books. I didn't read these when they first came out, so I figured I would give them a shot. I am SO GLAD that I did! These books are really funny and smart, they have romance AND action both (LOTS of both!) so they could appeal to many different people. I was surprised how real the characters seemed to me. I like that Claire </span>
  <span id="freeText7535129899445735260" style="display:none">So, I was totally srprised by how much I LOVED these books! I checked them out of my library warily because I've been so burned out on vampires after the recent craze in YA books. I didn't read these when they first came out, so I figured I would give them a shot. I am SO GLAD that I did! These books are really funny and smart, they have romance AND action both (LOTS of both!) so they could appeal to many different people. I was surprised how real the characters seemed to me. I like that Claire is practically a genius, but she doesn't think she knows everything. I can't wait to read the rest of the books in this series that have been published so far. I will wait for the ones yet to be published eagerly. I would recommend this series to anyone that likes well-written supernatural fiction. Bonus factor is that this is in a college setting rather than high school! I will most DEFINITELY be buying my own copies of these books and will re-read them many times! :)</span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cal (Cal&#39;s Reading Corner)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cal (Cal&#39;s Reading Corner)" href="/user/show/23055103-cal-cal-s-reading-corner">Cal (Cal&#39;s Reading Corner)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1917491207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3907870837562025499">Read more bookish goodness on my book blog: <a href='https://thehyperlapse.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cal's YA Reads</a><br/><br/>4/5 stars.<br/><br/>Okay so this book started off as a 2/5 stars, but slowly reached a 4 stars. That's pretty impressive, but I'm determined to give this series a go as a friend of mine gave all of her copies to me for free. <br/><br/>Claire is the worst protag for the first bit, but finally develops a personality by the second book (I read a '2 in 1' Volume).<br/><br/>I honestly believed Michael was going to be Claire's love interest, so I have a bit of underlying di</span>
  <span id="freeText3907870837562025499" style="display:none">Read more bookish goodness on my book blog: <a href="https://thehyperlapse.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cal's YA Reads</a><br /><br />4/5 stars.<br /><br />Okay so this book started off as a 2/5 stars, but slowly reached a 4 stars. That's pretty impressive, but I'm determined to give this series a go as a friend of mine gave all of her copies to me for free. <br /><br />Claire is the worst protag for the first bit, but finally develops a personality by the second book (I read a '2 in 1' Volume).<br /><br />I honestly believed Michael was going to be Claire's love interest, so I have a bit of underlying disappointment. We are teased constantly from Claire's thoughts… and poof-- He ends up with Eve??? Even though it was established at the start that she had a crush on Shane? <br /><br />I thought the Glass House roommates (Eve, Shane and Michael) were A LOT like Alice, Emmett, and Edward (before I realised he wasn't the main love interest). That's all I see them as, really. <br /><br />I found it really interesting how Claire struggles with Monica. It was nice, as weird as it is to say, to see bullying exist in current books. I usually never come across it, except for my dear love; Vampire Academy (with the dreaded Mia-- or shall we say; Mee-UGH). Monica was a hardcore bully too-- not just usual bitchy queens with simple words. It's awful what she did but I like the writing! Well done, Caine.<br /><br />I'll read the following sequels, for sure. It's not something I'm terribly invested in. That may be because I'm so disappointed at Shane being the love interest--- AFTER ALL THAT BUILD UP OF HIM VIEWING HER LIKE A SISTER, frankly; I'm disgusted. Ohhhh well. Embrace the cliches, I tell myself, this is a moderately decent vampire series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3907870837562025499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_196326153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/196326153" />
    <a title="Marybeth " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5281063-marybeth"><img alt="Marybeth " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389062199p2/5281063.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/196326153?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marybeth " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marybeth " href="/user/show/5281063-marybeth">Marybeth </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5281063-marybeth?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5281063-marybeth?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer196326153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17475864353129356411"> I actually never heard of the MORGANVILLE VAMPIRES before, and I picked up this book because, honestly, I liked the cover. It was pretty and a little mysterious and dark and I knew it obviously had something to do with vampires.<br/><br/>I wasn't sure I was going to like it at first and I was glad when I had the first two books in one, because I really did like it. Claire is smart, Eve is funny, Shane is the tough guy, and Michael is basically the head of it all, and they all connect so well together, it</span>
  <span id="freeText17475864353129356411" style="display:none"> I actually never heard of the MORGANVILLE VAMPIRES before, and I picked up this book because, honestly, I liked the cover. It was pretty and a little mysterious and dark and I knew it obviously had something to do with vampires.<br /><br />I wasn't sure I was going to like it at first and I was glad when I had the first two books in one, because I really did like it. Claire is smart, Eve is funny, Shane is the tough guy, and Michael is basically the head of it all, and they all connect so well together, it was wonderful.<br /><br />There were a lot of portions I laughed, and some parts where I literally thought that this should not belong in the YA section. The plot-line feels unbelievably complex but when when paying attention it's actually just really well planned out. The books aren't too long and their not too short, and there's actual character development throughout.<br /><br />I had moments where my jaw dropped, I was scared, and I was biting my nails in anticipation. I was sad when it ended and was ready to rush out to get the next volume, but I don't have it yet.<br /><br />The story didn't go too fast nor too slow, and the world that Rachel made was fantastic. Again, I'm sure I'm one of the few people left in this world who has yet to read it, but I'm glad I did. I also love how Rachel ends each book with a cliffhanger of sorts.<br /><br />Twisted, dark, mysterious, and funny. If you have yet to get this book, it is highly recommended that you do. You will not regret it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17475864353129356411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_130225956" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130225956" />
    <a title="Michelle  novelsontherun" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3677193-michelle-novelsontherun"><img alt="Michelle  novelsontherun" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1381731236p2/3677193.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130225956?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle  novelsontherun" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle  novelsontherun" href="/user/show/3677193-michelle-novelsontherun">Michelle  novelsontherun</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130225956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer808677674412767923">RATING: 4 STARS!!<br/><br/>GLASS HOUSES<br/><br/>I really liked the title of this book, in relation to the story, the first book in the kick vampire butt , series. It had a couple meanings, you will have to read the book to find out. <br/><br/>Who knew having your laundry stolen would turn into 11 titled books , to date. ( Bite Club # 10, releases May 2nd 2011, Last Breath # 11 , releases 1st November 2011) <br/><br/>Claire Danvers, female lead, 16 nearly 17yrs old ( she likes to remind Shane & Michael), has got herself in a rather de</span>
  <span id="freeText808677674412767923" style="display:none">RATING: 4 STARS!!<br /><br />GLASS HOUSES<br /><br />I really liked the title of this book, in relation to the story, the first book in the kick vampire butt , series. It had a couple meanings, you will have to read the book to find out. <br /><br />Who knew having your laundry stolen would turn into 11 titled books , to date. ( Bite Club # 10, releases May 2nd 2011, Last Breath # 11 , releases 1st November 2011) <br /><br />Claire Danvers, female lead, 16 nearly 17yrs old ( she likes to remind Shane &amp; Michael), has got herself in a rather deadly pickle with Monica Morell , ( queen bitchie) on her campus. It doesn’t take much to be targeted by Monica and the Monickettes and she doesn’t forgive or forget , she will hunt you down and inflict pain..... or worse.<br /><br />Cue missing laundry....<br /><br />Survival mode kicks in and Claire takes charge of her battered life and answers an advert to share accommodation.<br /><br />Enter , Eve , the gothic chick, Shane and the mysterious Michael who brings a whole new meaning to the graveyard shift.<br /><br />Eve, has quite a casual attitude towards the dangers lurking, until she realises how close to her doorstep they really are. She has a good heart, maybe too trustworthy. Eve works nights at ‘Common Ground’ cafe, her ‘hippee’ boss Oliver, is always looking out for her.<br /><br />Michael is the head of the house and the mature, sensible one. Shane appears a bit of a slacker, but he will have your back if you need it.<br /><br />The small College town of Morganville is not what it seems. It has very, very dark secrets. Morganville is not safe after dark, unless you have protection, even that can be revoked.<br /><br />Shane has seen some very dark days of his own and only knows too well the dangers, lurking. Claire is oblivious but is a fast learner. She has to be.<br /><br />Shane isn’t looking for trouble, Claire can’t help but bring trouble, now Shane is endeavouring to keep them both out of trouble. Mysterious Michael can only do so much. <br /><br />There’s something the vampires want, Claire pulls a Nancy Drew, does some creative snooping, all is revealed, so she thinks... who knew going to College was this difficult.<br /><br />I really enjoyed Glass Houses. There were a couple wobbly bits in the storyline, but hey , 10 books later Rachel is still writing this series, obviously the storyline really grows and the characters really grow. <br /><br />There is no real romance, some looks between characters, hand holding, bit of smooching, but Claire is ‘jail bait’ , so understandable.<br /><br />‘Glass Houses’ , is more world building, getting to know the characters, establishing why humans even live in Morganville when they know vampires rule Morganville . <br /><br />The latter half of the book, the pace really picked up and the ending, AAGGghhhGGhhh!! Bit of a cliffhanger. <br /><br />I usually have a Team guy that is on my t-shirt by the end of a book. I don't really have my Team guy from this book...hopefully I will have a Team guy by end of The Dead Girls Dance....* walks off ..sad face* ..teamless...hee..hee.<br /><br />I’m glad I have 8 more books lined up ready to read, no waiting!!! Plus ‘Bite Club ‘ releasing May 2nd 2011.<br /><br />I can’t wait to read how the story unfolds and grows in Rachel’s vampire town and where she takes her characters . I’ve already cracked open book # 2 , ‘The Dead Girls Dance’....... intriguing title.<br /><br /><br />THE DEAD GIRL'S DANCE<br /><br />RATING: 4 DANGEROUS STARS!!!<br /><br />I couldn’t help thinking when reading this 2nd instalment in The Morganville Vampires series that I would have liked part of this book to have been tacked onto ‘Glass Houses’, to me personally , it would have given me that extra character depth I was missing from ‘Glass Houses’. Mind you my thoughts are quite redundant in a way as I have no great time lapse between the next 9 books. I can just merrily read one after the other so my thoughts are cleared up almost straight away. Let me explain myself better. Maybe it has to do with the fact that I am currently reading the books in volumes = 2 books per volume. So it’s kind of like I am reading one big book with a bit of an interval in between. I really enjoyed ‘Glass Houses’, but what I read in ‘The Dead Girls’ Dance’, had some great character depth with Shane that I was missing from ‘Glass Houses’. I really ‘felt’ Shane as a character better in ‘The Dead Girls’ Dance’, amongst other things. If Glass Houses had been longer I would have been more satisfied with book 1. I really enjoyed book 1 , but I ‘felt’ book 2 and its characters much better.<br /><br />There is a whole lot of suspense, anxious moments in ‘The Dead Girl’s Dance’. I really wanted to slap Monica and the Monickettes, HARD!! These girls are uber dangerous. Crikey, they needed to be pulled off that pedestal.<br /><br />Shane’s father , I can understand his state of mind with his daughter and wife, but I think his mind may have crossed the line into forgetting he has a son, somebody that he should be loving ,not pushing away with blind fury and possibly ending up a bit unstable in the brain department. His devotion to his cause is getting out of control. It’s hurting who he should love, deeply and his methods!!!<br /><br />I love Eve, even more in this book. She is just a wonderful character who will do anything for anybody in the house, if they are in danger or need her help. She is a stand up character, she has your back.<br /><br />Amelie is an intriguing character. I feel safe with her, but should I?<br /><br />I really like the human detectives Lowe and Hess. They helped me to believe that all is not corrupt amongst the humans living in Morganville. There is hope that humans can help each other, aren't afraid to try and do the small bit they can.<br /><br />The storyline was fast paced , exciting, suspenseful, dangerous and I really enjoyed it. There was some romance, more hot smooches, relationships are forming. We learn more of the magic, I suppose you could say, of the vampire world. <br /><br />I am a titles girl. I like the title of books to mean something to the story. The Dead Girl’s Dance, is a real cool title, but it was such a small part of the story. When I read the title of the book I imagined something a lot different, lol!! Just a personal observation.<br /><br />Claire’s character had me just so anxious in his book, as she ran from person to person trying to get the help she needed. I felt as desperate as she felt. I was there for Claire..loL!! I was egging her on. When one dead end faced her, she looked for another opening, anything that would help Shane. I was even trying to think how to get Shane out of his pickle. Rachel had me turning the pages feverishly as I hoped for a solution, but kept getting dead ends for Shane’s safety. <br /><br />Michael, what has he gone and done!!! <br /><br />What will Claire do to keep everybody safe????<br /><br />When reading , I felt like Morganville was the only place on earth. Everyone is surviving Morganville and it’s dangers. I didn’t feel like any other place existed, but Morganville. <br /><br />Rachel has me trapped ...lol!! I can’t even imagine where the next 8 books will take me. * whispers* I don’t think I will be leaving Morganville ........<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="808677674412767923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_77899381" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77899381" />
    <a title="Justin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2027950-justin"><img alt="Justin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428434221p2/2027950.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77899381?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/2027950-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2027950-justin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2027950-justin?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77899381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1480890929076966182">I pretty much avoid sparkly vampire stories. I’ve never read Twilight, and have not seen the movies. I am only vaguely familiar with Anne Rice’s stuff. I have been “self-sheltered” from fantasy vampire fiction. When I seen that Penguin Books (NAL Trade) was going to do a re-release of Rachel Caine’s The Morganville Vampires in a 2 in 1 format….. I asked for a copy. I wanted to get a feel for this whole area of fantasy I’ve had no clue about. As a reviewer I felt somewhat obligated to at least tr</span>
  <span id="freeText1480890929076966182" style="display:none">I pretty much avoid sparkly vampire stories. I’ve never read Twilight, and have not seen the movies. I am only vaguely familiar with Anne Rice’s stuff. I have been “self-sheltered” from fantasy vampire fiction. When I seen that Penguin Books (NAL Trade) was going to do a re-release of Rachel Caine’s The Morganville Vampires in a 2 in 1 format….. I asked for a copy. I wanted to get a feel for this whole area of fantasy I’ve had no clue about. As a reviewer I felt somewhat obligated to at least try it. The two books I read were both written from the perspective of 16 (almost 17!) year old Claire Danvers. Claire is an exceptionally smart girl who is has been placed in college early. She wanted to go to Yale or MIT, but before her parents will allow her to live on the other side of the country they are making her do a two year term at the not so far away college in Morganville, Texas. This proves to be a rather unwise decision on the part of her parents, as Morganville happens to have a lot of vampires. Our little Claire ends up in the thick of them rather quickly.<br /><br /> In book one Glass Houses, Claire is getting harassed and beaten by other girls in her dorm, so she takes refuge in an off campus house with 3 other roommates. Claire and her three roommates become the four central characters of the story, as they try to avoid pissing off the local vampires while unraveling the bloody secrets of Morganville. Book two, The Dead Girl’s Dance falls directly behind Glass Houses. There is no gap of time between the two. The first book literally ends in the middle of a knife swing and book two starts with the conclusion of the knife swing. The Dead Girl’s Dance continues the story by getting the foursome deeper into the vampire doodoo, and it gets actually kind of fun imagining exactly how they are going to get out of it with out nuking the entire town. <br /><br />Morganville Vampires books are definitely intended for teenage girls. I suffered through several detailed descriptions of hunky dudes with windblown hair, various shoe selections, and lots of kissy face action. I knew what I was going to get some of that when I picked this up, and to be honest none of the girly stuff was that overdone. I felt that Rachael Caine wrote the extremely smart 16 year old perspective rather well. I have only a few real complaints. Most of the gripes being within the first book. In Glass Houses all the characters except Claire felt a bit shallow, and the plot felt rushed. It’s almost as if Ms. Caine needed to get this opening book out of the way in order to get into the more juicy bits of her story starting in book two. In The Dead Girl’s Dance several characters go through changes that bring them more depth. The plot is more complicated and feels more cohesive than the first. I wondered whether these two books were originally written together and then later separated before submitted for publishing, because it certainly feels that way.<br /><br />I enjoyed The Morganville Vampire books, even though I’m way outside the intended demographic. I think it’s safe to recommend them to any fantasy fan that needs a break from their usual faire. I definitely recommend them to our teenage readers. I would advise parents read to them first, especially if your young one is under 15 or 16. There is some suggestive content, but all of it well within a PG rating. There are 7 of these books out now, with #8 on the way. I hope Penguin plans on publishing the rest in the 2 for 1 package, for it makes it a worthy purchase.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1480890929076966182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_178151101" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178151101" />
    <a title="Whitney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3827678-whitney"><img alt="Whitney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580343008p2/3827678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178151101?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney" href="/user/show/3827678-whitney">Whitney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3827678-whitney?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3827678-whitney?shelf=all-time-faves">all-time-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3827678-whitney?shelf=surprised-as-hell">surprised-as-hell</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3827678-whitney?shelf=kickass-heroes">kickass-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3827678-whitney?shelf=actually-pretty-good">actually-pretty-good</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178151101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16529887707666964656">Oh, vampires. It sounds cliche nowadays, doesn't it? Well, this book puts a whole new perspective to vampires. Sure, it has the usual things with them; bloodsucking, burning in sunlight, holy water, crosses, silver, etc. But I thought it was cool how they made a contract with someone that binds them to that vampire forever, or until they say so. They have to abide by their rules, who to marry, when to get married, if you can have children or not. It's pretty intense if you ask moi. I know it's w</span>
  <span id="freeText16529887707666964656" style="display:none">Oh, vampires. It sounds cliche nowadays, doesn't it? Well, this book puts a whole new perspective to vampires. Sure, it has the usual things with them; bloodsucking, burning in sunlight, holy water, crosses, silver, etc. But I thought it was cool how they made a contract with someone that binds them to that vampire forever, or until they say so. They have to abide by their rules, who to marry, when to get married, if you can have children or not. It's pretty intense if you ask moi. I know it's weird when I say it's cool, but it's new. I like new stuff. :3 Especially with vampires...since they're so cliche now. <i>
  <s>Thanks, Stephenie Meyer.</s>
</i><br><br>I really liked the fact that Michael was a...ghost thing...in the beginning. I've had this series on my shelf for a long time now, and I thought he was a vampire this whole time. I was going on what people said about the series and stuff, and that's what I got out of it lol. So that put a cog in my wheel lol. But then it started to turn in the second part of the book. (Meaning the second book since there's two books in one.) Michael was a sweetheart on up in the book. I didn't like him at first, since he was being an asshole to Claire about moving into their mansion that looks like "<i>Gone with the Wind</i> meets <i>The Munsters</i>." :P<br><br>And when I say "their mansion," I mean by the trio that lives there. Shane, Eve, and Michael. And I love Shane. The end. He's just...urgh. I love him. xD Eve is an awesome character. She has to be the second character that I've "met" that's a pure Goth, if you will. LOL. I loved her, she was funny. &lt;3 Also, can I say that I will <b>
  <i>NEVER</i>
</b> remotely like Monica...EVER...AT ALL? I don't give a shit if she sprouts wings and turns into an angel and saves everybody at the end of the series. I will forever hate that bitch. :) I was on Eve's side when she said, "<i>Maybe she does deserve a good blowtorching.</i>" And Claire's like, "<i>No. Nobody deserves that.</i>" And I'm sitting here like: <a href="http://s350.photobucket.com/albums/q415/whitney12339/GIFS/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_lpuf88pzSC1qe53o2.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380351824ra/705386.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I was about to die towards the end when Shane <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[was about to get burned alive <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <i>I about cried myself to death.</i> I really love Shane, I just hope he doesn't piss me off in the books to come in this series.<br><br>Okay. I'm done. All-in-all this was a fantastic book. I can't wait to read the next ones! I pretty much recommend this book to anyone who likes vampires. On the cover of the omnibus that I have, it says, "<i>Fans of Twilight will love this.</i>" ...Sure, that's true. But this is nothing close to Twilight, just so you know. It's a WHOLE LOT BETTER. :D</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16529887707666964656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102009333" />
    <a title="Morgan F" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2941288-morgan-f"><img alt="Morgan F" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262298598p2/2941288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102009333?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morgan F" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morgan F" href="/user/show/2941288-morgan-f">Morgan F</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=2000s">2000s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=characters-i-wanna-shoot">characters-i-wanna-shoot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=suckfest">suckfest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=pretty-covers">pretty-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=its-a-girl">its-a-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=good-sized">good-sized</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102009333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10706423469625881913">I wanted to like this one. I really did. It seemed like it was made for me. Morganville? Morgan? You can't ignore the connection. But sadly I was disappointed.<br/><br/>The volume I read was an omnibus of the first two books. I wish I just would've bought the first one. The series is about Claire Danvers, a 16 yr old student living in the college town of Morganville. She moves into the Glass House, but not all her roommates might be living. She soon finds out that Morganville is no ordinary college town, </span>
  <span id="freeText10706423469625881913" style="display:none">I wanted to like this one. I really did. It seemed like it was made for me. Morganville? Morgan? You can't ignore the connection. But sadly I was disappointed.<br /><br />The volume I read was an omnibus of the first two books. I wish I just would've bought the first one. The series is about Claire Danvers, a 16 yr old student living in the college town of Morganville. She moves into the Glass House, but not all her roommates might be living. She soon finds out that Morganville is no ordinary college town, but one infested with vampires.<br /><br />I strongly disliked Claire. Very strongly. I mean, what was the purpose of making her 16? To make her even more annoying?? She was immature and whiny and......*simmers down*. In the second book, all the other characters were like "Oh, what happened to the little mousy girl?", I would go "She's right here guys. Just because its a new book doesn't mean she underwent a personality change." <br /><br />The other characters were somewhat unlikable. Out all of them, I liked Michael the best. I wish he could have been the love interest. Which brings me to Shane......I just don't get his appeal. He's just some hotheaded "gorgeous" guy. I don't like him. I wish he would have been torched. Him and Claire were just so awkwardly matched. It seemed forced to me. After little to no interaction, Claire is all up in his lap calling him her boyfriend (although that didn't stop her from going on that date with Ian). The romance between them was gag-worthy, honestly. The whole "let's play baseball thing". Yuck. And of course they can't <i>really</i> do it, because of the age difference. Gotta build up that sexual tension.<br /><br />And, sorry for all the people who liked this series, I'm going to be hatin' on the writing now. It was bad. Real bad. It didn't make any sense. It was in third person, but wanted to be in first person. Pick a POV already!!! I had the most difficul time trying to figure out who was speaking or acting at any given time. And Caine would put <i>random</i> words in italics to <i>prove</i> a <i>point</i>. They were <i>everywhere</i>.<br /><br />And some of the action didn't have a purpse. It seems Caine would just get bored and go "hhhmmmm, let's go over here now so we can over-complicate things!!" <br /><br />The main problem was I never was emotionally invested enough. I didn't care what happened. It never held me in suspense. I was just waiting for it to be over.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10706423469625881913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_546733618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/546733618" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/546733618?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=vampires-related">vampires-related</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=young-adult-books">young-adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=supernatural-stuff">supernatural-stuff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer546733618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14435960419472013275">The story takes place in a Texas small town Morganville, unbeknownst to outsiders, the town was secretly ran by vampires and humans were treated as second class citizens and bloodbank on two legs. The heroine Claire was a very smart 16 years old girl leaving home to study in an university next to Morganville, only to find herself the easy target of school bullies and worse, she was also being dragged into the troubles between vampires and humans in town. Luckily she wasn’t alone, Claire found he</span>
  <span id="freeText14435960419472013275" style="display:none">The story takes place in a Texas small town Morganville, unbeknownst to outsiders, the town was secretly ran by vampires and humans were treated as second class citizens and bloodbank on two legs. The heroine Claire was a very smart 16 years old girl leaving home to study in an university next to Morganville, only to find herself the easy target of school bullies and worse, she was also being dragged into the troubles between vampires and humans in town. Luckily she wasn’t alone, Claire found her sanctuary in The Glass House, and a small band of ‘free’ humans (who didn’t take protection and orders from vampires) Michael Glass, the current young owner of the Glass House; Eve the friendly Goth girl, Shane the hothead guy with a painful past.<br /><br />It’s a nice story, with a crew of likable, down to earth characters, who were being pushed through one deadly situation after another. The troubles which the residents in the Glass House had gotten themselves into are too many that it is almost humorous (in a good way). And I really like how the author wrote her vampires, they were brutal, cunning and at some point very cold blooded, but their characters were built that way with reasons, and you soon can tell the truly evil ones from the rest. The vampires aren’t all bad but they are not humans’ harmless best friends either. I think it’s what made Rachel Caine’s novels realistic<br /><br />The human characters are as well written as the vampires too. After reading the books you almost hope you have friends like Michael, Eve and Shane. Claire…she is okay but I think she’s too stubborn to a point of pathetic when she foolishly kept insisting on going to school when she knew her life is in danger. The same thing happened too many times and you have to start wonder why that supposedly smart girl seemingly still hadn’t learned her lesson.<br /><br />I also like how love relationships and sex are handled in the story. Hell, at least no one is dying to be turned into a vampire after she realizes her boyfriend had become a member of the undead.<br /><br />On the backcover of the novel, there was a quote from SFX Magazine: <b>DUMP MEYER’S TWILIGHT BOOKS AND REPLACE THEM WITH THE MORGANVILLES.</b> I really, really can’t agree more!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14435960419472013275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15196912789186175646">THIS REVIEW CONTAINS SPOILERS SO BACK OFF BEFORE YOU HATE ME SO MUCH. <br/><br/>I actually read this book two years ago. I reread the book yesterday and finished it this morning.   <span id="freeText15196912789186175646" style="display:none">THIS REVIEW CONTAINS SPOILERS SO BACK OFF BEFORE YOU HATE ME SO MUCH. <br /><br />I actually read this book two years ago. I reread the book yesterday and finished it this morning. What makes it so special that I keep reading this series is that IT IS SO DIFFERENT FROM TWILIGHT /YAS FINALLY I WANNA SEE OTHER VAMPIRES' POV FGS/ <br /><br />I kinda like how the whole 'Protection' thing is going on in the story. I really like how the houses in the Morganville use 'permissions' to welcome their guests. That is freaking awesome; and let say you hate your guests, you can at anytime revoke the house access from your guests and automatically your guests will be kicked out from your house /I REALLY LIKE THE HOUSES, ESPECIALLY THE GLASS HOUSE/ <br /><br />I SHIP CLAIRE AND SHANE OMG THEY'RE SO FUDGING CUTE LIKE SO CUTE WHEN I'M PICTURING THEM TOGETHER. As for Eve and Michael, yeah yeah whatever I don't mind anything. Do whatever you guys want hahaha. <br /><br />Okay so here's the bad part. I was expecting the Michael 'changing' moment to be sooooo epic and bizarre. Like he's trembling for life or gasping for air that obviously he's the one who has the problem while we horrendously looking at him; waiting and hoping that he will not die, fuh. But instead they skip that part badly and how they settle the so-called ceremony is just by letting Michael sucking on the founder's blood. What? Sucks!!!! <br /><br />But I think the most heartbreaking moment is when she opt for the founder's offer to claim safety for her and her friends. How brave of her. Even though the scene is just merely a page but I really understand the feeling, the intense going on. <br /><br />All in all, I give this book 4.3 stars! Keep up! </span>

<div id="review_121538768" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121538768" />
    <a title="Yin Chien 인첸" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2944417-yin-chien"><img alt="Yin Chien 인첸" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1322927134p2/2944417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121538768?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yin Chien 인첸" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yin Chien 인첸" href="/user/show/2944417-yin-chien">Yin Chien 인첸</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121538768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3512149679324124568">I was immediately attracted by this book. Somehow, I feel connected to the protagonist, Claire Danvers because of her geeky (and a little bit nerdy) style. I'd also like to compliment the cover - it's really eye-catching<br/><br/>Rachel is really good at delivering the story, because she makes me feel the anger, worries and fear of the characters in the story. The characters are well-developed and I can get an exact idea of their personalities. You will find out that you must keep on reading to unravel th</span>
  <span id="freeText3512149679324124568" style="display:none">I was immediately attracted by this book. Somehow, I feel connected to the protagonist, Claire Danvers because of her geeky (and a little bit nerdy) style. I'd also like to compliment the cover - it's really eye-catching<br /><br />Rachel is really good at delivering the story, because she makes me feel the anger, worries and fear of the characters in the story. The characters are well-developed and I can get an exact idea of their personalities. You will find out that you must keep on reading to unravel the mystery behind all the strange, unusual happenings. And when you do, somehow you'll feel like there's more to come. I didn't realize the who bad guy was at the beginning, because he seems so bright, cheerful and warm. I guess we can't judge a person by his appearance. Rachel also introduced vampire politics, in which influential vampires have great power and high statuses. Humans (such as cops) actually have to put themselves at the vampires' disposal. Now this is something new to me. <br /><br />In The Dead Girls' Dance, there are some dangerous situations. Shane is wrongly accused of killing a vampire and is to be burned to death. Claire and her friends has to race against time to find a way to rescue Shane. I'm really impressed when I read about how Claire fought back when she was nearly raped by a gang of good-for-nothings, even when she was drugged at that time. I'm curious to see what will happen next!<br /><br />In a nutshell, this novel is suspenseful, fast-paced and exciting. Highly recommended to teenagers who love reading about the undead.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3512149679324124568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6519364090654661174" style="display:none">Ohhhh my gosh this book had me pulling out my hair. I don't bash books or authors because I don't have a talent for writing so I read.. But this book was really really really and I mean really lame. If your bored and you don't have anything better to read then pick up this book but if you have something better around you then don't. <span id="freeTextContainer2263477884546415702">Glass House:<br/>Vampires are real, and a lot of them live in Morganville, Texas. Claire Danvers is a sixteen year old college freshmen, and after getting tired of being bullied all the time, she seeks out a place to live off campus, stumbling across the Glass house. In this book, history unravels itself in front Claire and her new roommates, Michael Glass, Eve Rosser, and Shane Collins. This first book of the Morganville Vampires series is definitely an eye catcher and will have you begging more.<br/>The</span>
  <span id="freeText2263477884546415702" style="display:none">Glass House:<br />Vampires are real, and a lot of them live in Morganville, Texas. Claire Danvers is a sixteen year old college freshmen, and after getting tired of being bullied all the time, she seeks out a place to live off campus, stumbling across the Glass house. In this book, history unravels itself in front Claire and her new roommates, Michael Glass, Eve Rosser, and Shane Collins. This first book of the Morganville Vampires series is definitely an eye catcher and will have you begging more.<br />The Dead Girls' Dance:<br />Claire is finally getting used to the fact that vampires exist and are living in Morganville, Texas when she and her roommate Eve get invited to the Dead Girls' Dance. While Claire and her roommates try to do everything they can to get Shane back, Michael's grandfather steps into the picture to lend a hand. In this second installment by Rachel Caine, new stories and problems are sure to come, and you'll never see them coming. I definitely recommend this book to you if you're into sci-fi mysteries, because it'll most definitely leave you hungry for more.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText8348769131997996261" style="display:none">I finished the first half today...(since this book has the first two books combined). It started out a bit slow and rough. I had to make myself keep reading through the first couple of chapters as it took some time to get my bearings in the story, figure out the key characters, and the basic backdrop for the series. But I am glad I did! I am intrigued by the idea of a whole town basically run by vampires, the different factions of vampires, and how a human survives (or doesn't) in this small strange town.<br /><br />Finished the second half, or the second book last night. It was pretty good. Like most stories, you could see the final conflict coming, but there were a few twists and turns along the way that were surprising and added to the overall story. I am interested to see where this world of vampires goes, so off to the library I go for the next book! </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer182237370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15459677832250888627"> The best thing about this book (these books?) is that it deviates from all the common plot points that are becoming normal parts of so many YA books nowadays--there're no love triangles, a completely different take on vampires, and a dangerously mysterious town with a frightening hierarchy of species. Although Claire is a new type of protagonist, a bookish sixteen-year-old genius who's already a freshman in college, she definitely has pluck and a protective loyalty towards her friends and famil</span>
  <span id="freeText15459677832250888627" style="display:none"> The best thing about this book (these books?) is that it deviates from all the common plot points that are becoming normal parts of so many YA books nowadays--there're no love triangles, a completely different take on vampires, and a dangerously mysterious town with a frightening hierarchy of species. Although Claire is a new type of protagonist, a bookish sixteen-year-old genius who's already a freshman in college, she definitely has pluck and a protective loyalty towards her friends and family. The character development is great; I love the other main characters, Michael, Shane, and Eve, and the remaining characters are just as well-crafted. Caine has a writing style that just draws you in; the mystery, unexpected twists, and gritty action are just added bonuses. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15459677832250888627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2642789121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7590959321242737747">Glass Houses Review:<br/><br/>I am officially a Rachel Caine fan. I read one of her other books before, and I liked it, but not as much as I loved this book. Her writing style appealed to me more in this book, and I was hooked pretty much in the first couple of pages.<br/> <br/>This book had one of the key things I think every wonderful book has-a great group of friends that the story revolves around. They're my favorite things to read about, and I love reading their interactions and jokes and everything else. It a</span>
  <span id="freeText7590959321242737747" style="display:none">Glass Houses Review:<br /><br />I am officially a Rachel Caine fan. I read one of her other books before, and I liked it, but not as much as I loved this book. Her writing style appealed to me more in this book, and I was hooked pretty much in the first couple of pages.<br /> <br />This book had one of the key things I think every wonderful book has-a great group of friends that the story revolves around. They're my favorite things to read about, and I love reading their interactions and jokes and everything else. It also didn't hurt that I love each of the characters individually-I love Claire, the extremely smart, sweet, and relatable main character who always tries to do the right thing for her friends! And sassy Eve, with her epic style and hilarious personality and comebacks! And my gosh, Shane and Michael? I love Shane in all his protective, sarcastic handsomeness. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He and Claire are a lovely couple and I hope they stay together for the entire series-but something tells me they will(hehe). And the same goes for Eve and Michael. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Michael is a great friend, and he always wants to keep everyone safe. Shane and Michael's friendship also makes me very happy-their personalities compliment each other extremely well.<br /><br />The plot also was perfect for everyone to come together and trust each other and form and awesome vampire-fighting squad! I loved everyone being together in the same house-it was a great way for them to all form good relationships with each other-(<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ and I loved at the end when they were all defending the house from the vampires and Oliver (who I hate so much! And Monica, too! I detest Monica.)and everyone was being all epic and fierce-warrior-like-which reminds me. Amelie was interesting. I'm glad she saved them all, but I'm also still very wary of her <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />So. Pretty much, what you need to know is that this is a book worth picking up. If you like vampires and romance, I highly recommend this to you-and I don't think you'll be disappointed. :):):):):)<br /><br />Now, on to Dead Girls' Dance:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ WARNING. DO NOT READ THIS REVIEW IF YOU HAVE NOT READ GLASS HOUSES AND DEAD GIRL'S DANCE.<br /><br />Well, I've already said I loved this book from the start. This book only furthered my love for the Morganville vampires. I want this review to be shorter, so let me make this quick; I love the freaky-awesome characters and the sweet relationships-Claire is super awesome and very real, and quite frankly a fantastic main character, along with her bestie, Eve, who is super snazzy and hysterical. Shane and Michael both hold my heart, and they are so sweet and funny, and their whole group makes my soul happy. The plot was so twisty and unexpected, with Michael's death and vampirism, and Sam, who I like in spite of his vampirism, and stupid Oliver and stupid Frank Collins and Claire signing the contract and basically everyone almost dying! This was a great sequel to Glass Houses-and this is a super long series, which is awesome because it just keeps getting better every book! :):):):):)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /></span>

<div id="review_163285763" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163285763" />
    <a title="Novels On The Run" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4119908-novels-on-the-run"><img alt="Novels On The Run" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1281183501p2/4119908.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/163285763?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Novels On The Run" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Novels On The Run" href="/user/show/4119908-novels-on-the-run">Novels On The Run</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163285763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18294961529435450345">MICHELLE'S REVIEW:<br/><br/>RATING: 4 SHANE & MICHAEL STARS!!<br/><br/>I really liked the title of this book, in relation to the story, the first book in the kick vampire butt , series. It had a couple meanings, you will have to read the book to find out. <br/><br/>Who knew having your laundry stolen would turn into 11 titled books , to date. ( Bite Club # 10, releases May 2nd 2011, Last Breath # 11 , releases 1st November 2011) <br/><br/>Claire Danvers, female lead, 16 nearly 17yrs old ( she likes to remind Shane & Michael), has got </span>
  <span id="freeText18294961529435450345" style="display:none">MICHELLE'S REVIEW:<br /><br />RATING: 4 SHANE &amp; MICHAEL STARS!!<br /><br />I really liked the title of this book, in relation to the story, the first book in the kick vampire butt , series. It had a couple meanings, you will have to read the book to find out. <br /><br />Who knew having your laundry stolen would turn into 11 titled books , to date. ( Bite Club # 10, releases May 2nd 2011, Last Breath # 11 , releases 1st November 2011) <br /><br />Claire Danvers, female lead, 16 nearly 17yrs old ( she likes to remind Shane &amp; Michael), has got herself in a rather deadly pickle with Monica Morell , ( queen bitchie) on her campus. It doesn’t take much to be targeted by Monica and the Monickettes and she doesn’t forgive or forget , she will hunt you down and inflict pain..... or worse.<br /><br />Cue missing laundry....<br /><br />Survival mode kicks in and Claire takes charge of her battered life and answers an advert to share accommodation.<br /><br />Enter , Eve , the gothic chick, Shane and the mysterious Michael who brings a whole new meaning to the graveyard shift.<br /><br />Eve, has quite a casual attitude towards the dangers lurking, until she realises how close to her doorstep they really are. She has a good heart, maybe too trustworthy. Eve works nights at ‘Common Ground’ cafe, her ‘hippee’ boss Oliver, is always looking out for her.<br /><br />Michael is the head of the house and the mature, sensible one. Shane appears a bit of a slacker, but he will have your back if you need it.<br /><br />The small College town of Morganville is not what it seems. It has very, very dark secrets. Morganville is not safe after dark, unless you have protection, even that can be revoked.<br /><br />Shane has seen some very dark days of his own and only knows too well the dangers, lurking. Claire is oblivious but is a fast learner. She has to be.<br /><br />Shane isn’t looking for trouble, Claire can’t help but bring trouble, now Shane is endeavouring to keep them both out of trouble. Mysterious Michael can only do so much. <br /><br />There’s something the vampires want, Claire pulls a Nancy Drew, does some creative snooping, all is revealed, so she thinks... who knew going to College was this difficult.<br /><br />I really enjoyed Glass Houses. There were a couple wobbly bits in the storyline, but hey , 10 books later Rachel is still writing this series, obviously the storyline really grows and the characters really grow. <br /><br />There is no real romance, some looks between characters, hand holding, bit of smooching, but Claire is ‘jail bait’ , so understandable.<br /><br />‘Glass Houses’ , is more world building, getting to know the characters, establishing why humans even live in Morganville when they know vampires rule Morganville . <br /><br />The latter half of the book, the pace really picked up and the ending, AAGGghhhGGhhh!! Bit of a cliffhanger. <br /><br />I usually have a Team guy that is on my t-shirt by the end of a book. I don't really have my Team guy from this book...hopefully I will have a Team guy by end of The Dead Girls Dance....* walks off ..sad face* ..teamless...hee..hee.<br /><br />I’m glad I have 8 more books lined up ready to read, no waiting!!! Plus ‘Bite Club ‘ releasing May 2nd 2011.<br /><br />I can’t wait to read how the story unfolds and grows in Rachel’s vampire town and where she takes her characters . I’ve already cracked open book # 2 , ‘The Dead Girls Dance’....... intriguing title.<br /><br /><br />THE DEAD GIRL'S DANCE<br /><br />RATING : 4 DANGEROUS STARS!!!<br /><br />I couldn’t help thinking when reading this 2nd instalment in The Morganville Vampires series that I would have liked part of this book to have been tacked onto ‘Glass Houses’, to me personally , it would have given me that extra character depth I was missing from ‘Glass Houses’. Mind you my thoughts are quite redundant in a way as I have no great time lapse between the next 9 books. I can just merrily read one after the other so my thoughts are cleared up almost straight away. Let me explain myself better. Maybe it has to do with the fact that I am currently reading the books in volumes = 2 books per volume. So it’s kind of like I am reading one big book with a bit of an interval in between. I really enjoyed ‘Glass Houses’, but what I read in ‘The Dead Girls’ Dance’, had some great character depth with Shane that I was missing from ‘Glass Houses’. I really ‘felt’ Shane as a character better in ‘The Dead Girls’ Dance’, amongst other things. If Glass Houses had been longer I would have been more satisfied with book 1. I really enjoyed book 1 , but I ‘felt’ book 2 and its characters much better.<br /><br />There is a whole lot of suspense, anxious moments in ‘The Dead Girl’s Dance’. I really wanted to slap Monica and the Monickettes, HARD!! These girls are uber dangerous. Crikey, they needed to be pulled off that pedestal.<br /><br />Shane’s father , I can understand his state of mind with his daughter and wife, but I think his mind may have crossed the line into forgetting he has a son, somebody that he should be loving ,not pushing away with blind fury and possibly ending up a bit unstable in the brain department. His devotion to his cause is getting out of control. It’s hurting who he should love, deeply and his methods!!!<br /><br />I love Eve, even more in this book. She is just a wonderful character who will do anything for anybody in the house, if they are in danger or need her help. She is a stand up character, she has your back.<br /><br />Amelie is an intriguing character. I feel safe with her, but should I?<br /><br />I really like the human detectives Lowe and Hess. They helped me to believe that all is not corrupt amongst the humans living in Morganville. There is hope that humans can help each other, aren't afraid to try and do the small bit they can.<br /><br />The storyline was fast paced , exciting, suspenseful, dangerous and I really enjoyed it. There was some romance, more hot smooches, relationships are forming. We learn more of the magic, I suppose you could say, of the vampire world. <br /><br />I am a titles girl. I like the title of books to mean something to the story. The Dead Girl’s Dance, is a real cool title, but it was such a small part of the story. When I read the title of the book I imagined something a lot different, lol!! Just a personal observation.<br /><br />Claire’s character had me just so anxious in his book, as she ran from person to person trying to get the help she needed. I felt as desperate as she felt. I was there for Claire..loL!! I was egging her on. When one dead end faced her, she looked for another opening, anything that would help Shane. I was even trying to think how to get Shane out of his pickle. Rachel had me turning the pages feverishly as I hoped for a solution, but kept getting dead ends for Shane’s safety. <br /><br />Michael, what has he gone and done!!! <br /><br />What will Claire do to keep everybody safe????<br /><br />When reading , I felt like Morganville was the only place on earth. Everyone is surviving Morganville and it’s dangers. I didn’t feel like any other place existed, but Morganville. <br /><br />Rachel has me trapped ...lol!! I can’t even imagine where the next 8 books will take me. * whispers* I don’t think I will be leaving Morganville ........<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18294961529435450345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

    n = load.length,
    i = 0,
    go = function () {
      for (i = 0; i < n; i += 1) {
        script = d.createElement('SCRIPT');
        script.type = 'text/javascript';
        script.async = true;
        script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>
